4579<p id="_720" tabindex="-1">

4580Treatment of patients with advanced or recurrent rectal cancer depends on the location of the disease. </p>

4581<section id="_721">

4582<h3 id="_721_toc">

4583Treatment Options for Stage IV and Recurrent Rectal Cancer</h3>

4584<p id="_722" tabindex="-1">

4585Treatment options for stage IV and recurrent rectal cancer include the following:</p>

4586<div class="pdq-content-list">

4587<ol id="_723">

4588<li>

4589<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_724">

4590Surgery with or without chemotherapy or radiation therapy</a>

4591.</li>

4592<li>

4593<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_928">

4594Systemic therapy</a>

4595.</li>

4596<li>

4597<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1275">

4598Second-line chemotherapy</a>

4599.</li>

4600<li>

4601<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1278">

4602Immunotherapy</a>

4603.</li>

4604<li>

4605<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_980">

4606Palliative therapy</a>

4607.</li>

4608</ol>

4609</div>

4610<section id="_724">

4611<h4 id="_724_toc">

4612Surgery with or without chemotherapy or radiation therapy</h4>

4613<p id="_925" tabindex="-1">

4614For patients with locally recurrent, liver-only, or lung-only metastatic disease, surgical resection, if feasible, is the only potentially curative treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

46151</a>

4616] Patients with limited pulmonary metastasis, and patients with both pulmonary and hepatic metastasis, may also be considered for surgical resection, with 5-year survival possible in highly selected patients.[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

46172</a>

4618-<a href="#cit/section_8.5">

46195</a>

4620] The presence of hydronephrosis

4621associated with recurrence appears to be a contraindication to surgery with

4622curative intent.[<a href="#cit/section_8.6">

46236</a>

4624]</p>

4625<p id="_926" tabindex="-1">

4626Locally recurrent rectal cancer may be resectable, particularly if an

4627inadequate prior operation was performed. For patients with local recurrence

4628alone after an initial, attempted curative resection, aggressive local therapy

4629with repeat low anterior resection and coloanal anastomosis, abdominoperineal resection, or posterior or total pelvic exenteration can lead to long-term

4630disease-free survival.[<a href="#cit/section_8.7">

46317</a>

4632,<a href="#cit/section_8.8">

46338</a>

4634] </p>

4635<p id="_927" tabindex="-1">

4636The use of induction chemoradiation therapy for previously

4637nonirradiated patients with locally advanced pelvic recurrence (pelvic side-wall, sacral, and/or

4638adjacent organ involvement) may increase resectability and

4639allow for sphincter preservation.[<a href="#cit/section_8.9">

46409</a>

4641,<a href="#cit/section_8.10">

464210</a>

4643] Intraoperative radiation therapy in patients who underwent previous external-beam radiation therapy may improve local control in patients with locally recurrent disease, with acceptable morbidity.[<a href="#cit/section_8.11">

464411</a>

4645]</p>

4646</section>

4647<section id="_928">

4648<h4 id="_928_toc">

4649Systemic therapy</h4>

4650<p id="_929" tabindex="-1">

4651The following are U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA)-approved drugs that are used alone and in combination with other drugs for patients with metastatic colorectal cancer:</p>

4652<div class="pdq-content-list">

4653<ul id="_930">

4654<li>

4655<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_931">

4656Fluorouracil (5-FU)</a>

4657.</li>

4658<li>

4659<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_935">

4660Irinotecan</a>

4661.</li>

4662<li>

4663<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_935">

4664Oxaliplatin</a>

4665.</li>

4666<li>

4667<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_944">

4668Capecitabine</a>

4669.</li>

4670<li>

4671<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_951">

4672Bevacizumab</a>

4673.</li>

4674<li>

4675<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1115">

4676FOLFOXIRI (irinotecan, oxaliplatin, leucovorin [LV], and 5-FU)</a>

4677.</li>

4678<li>

4679<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_959">

4680Cetuximab</a>

4681.</li>

4682<li>

4683<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1138">

4684Aflibercept</a>

4685. </li>

4686<li>

4687<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1195">

4688Ramucirumab</a>

4689. </li>

4690<li>

4691<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_969">

4692Panitumumab</a>

4693. </li>

4694<li>

4695<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1127">

4696 Anti-epidermal growth factor receptor (EGFR) antibody versus anti-vascular endothelial growth factor (VEGF) antibody with first-line chemotherapy</a>

4697. </li>

4698<li>

4699<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1142">

4700Regorafenib</a>

4701. </li>

4702<li>

4703<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1146">

4704TAS-102</a>

4705. </li>

4706<li>

4707<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1267">

4708Encorafenib with cetuximab for patients with <em class="gene-name">

4709BRAF</em>

4710 V600E mutations</a>

4711.</li>

4712</ul>

4713</div>

4714<section id="_931">

4715<h5 id="_931_toc">

47165-FU</h5>

4717<p id="_932" tabindex="-1">

4718When 5-FU was the only active chemotherapy drug, trials in patients with locally advanced, unresectable, or metastatic disease demonstrated partial responses and prolongation of the time-to-progression (TTP) of disease,[<a href="#cit/section_8.12">

471912</a>

4720,<a href="#cit/section_8.13">

472113</a>

4722] and improved survival and quality of life

4723in patients who received chemotherapy versus best supportive care.[<a href="#cit/section_8.14">

472414</a>

4725-<a href="#cit/section_8.16">

472616</a>

4727]

4728Several trials have analyzed the activity and toxic effects of various 5-FU/LV regimens using different doses and administration schedules and showed essentially equivalent results with a median survival time in the approximately 12-month range.[<a href="#cit/section_8.17">

472917</a>

4730]</p>

4731</section>

4732<section id="_935">

4733<h5 id="_935_toc">

4734Irinotecan and oxaliplatin </h5>

4735<p id="_936" tabindex="-1">

4736Three randomized studies in patients with metastatic colorectal cancer demonstrated improved response rates, progression-free survival (PFS), and overall survival (OS) when irinotecan or oxaliplatin was combined with 5-FU/LV.[<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

473718</a>

4738-<a href="#cit/section_8.20">

473920</a>

4740]</p>

4741<p id="_937" tabindex="-1">

4742Evidence (irinotecan vs. oxaliplatin):</p>

4743<div class="pdq-content-list">

4744<ol id="_938">

4745<li>

4746An intergroup study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00003594">

4747NCCTG-N9741</a>

4748 [NCT00003594]) compared irinotecan/5-FU/LV (IFL) with oxaliplatin/LV/5-FU (FOLFOX4) in first-line treatment for patients with metastatic colorectal cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

474921</a>

4750][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4751Level of evidence A1</a>

4752] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4753<ul id="_939">

4754<li>

4755Patients assigned to FOLFOX4 experienced an improved PFS compared with patients randomly assigned to IFL (median, 8.7 months vs. 6.9 months; <em>

4756P</em>

4757 = .014; hazard ratio [HR], 0.74; 95% confidence interval [CI], 0.61&#8211;0.89) and OS (19.5 months vs. 15.0 months; <em>

4758P</em>

4759 = .001; HR, 0.66; 95% CI, 0.54&#8211;0.82).</li>

4760</ul>

4761</div>

4762</li>

4763<li>

4764Subsequently, two studies compared FOLFOX with LV/5-FU/irinotecan (FOLFIRI), and patients were allowed to cross over after progression on first-line therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.22">

476522</a>

4766,<a href="#cit/section_8.23">

476723</a>

4768][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4769Level of evidence B1</a>

4770] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4771<ul id="_940">

4772<li>

4773PFS and OS were identical between the treatment arms in both studies.</li>

4774</ul>

4775</div>

4776</li>

4777<li>

4778The Bolus, Infusional, or Capecitabine with Camptosar-Celecoxib (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00094965">

4779BICC-C</a>

4780 [NCT00094965]) trial evaluated several different irinotecan-based regimens in patients with previously untreated metastatic colorectal cancer: FOLFIRI, irinotecan plus bolus 5-FU/LV (mIFL), and capecitabine/irinotecan (CAPIRI).[<a href="#cit/section_8.24">

478124</a>

4782] The study randomly assigned 430 patients and was closed early due to poor accrual.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4783<ul id="_941">

4784<li>

4785The patients who received FOLFIRI had a better PFS than the patients who received either mIFL (7.6 months vs. 5.9 months; <em>

4786P</em>

4787 = .004) or CAPIRI (7.6 months vs. 5.8 months; <em>

4788P</em>

4789 = .015).</li>

4790<li>

4791Patients who received CAPIRI had the highest (grade 3 or higher) rates of nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, dehydration, and hand-foot syndrome.</li>

4792</ul>

4793</div>

4794</li>

4795</ol>

4796</div>

4797<p id="_942" tabindex="-1">

4798Since the publication of these studies, the use of either FOLFOX or FOLFIRI is considered acceptable for first-line treatment of patients with metastatic colorectal cancer. However, when using an irinotecan-based regimen as first-line treatment of metastatic colorectal cancer, FOLFIRI is preferred.[<a href="#cit/section_8.24">

479924</a>

4800][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4801Level of evidence B1</a>

4802]</p>

4803</section>

4804<section id="_944">

4805<h5 id="_944_toc">

4806Capecitabine</h5>

4807<p id="_1063" tabindex="-1">

4808Before the advent of multiagent chemotherapy, two randomized studies demonstrated that capecitabine was associated with equivalent efficacy when compared with the Mayo Clinic regimen of 5-FU/LV.[<a href="#cit/section_8.25">

480925</a>

4810,<a href="#cit/section_8.26">

481126</a>

4812][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4813Level of evidence A1</a>

4814]</p>

4815<p id="_945" tabindex="-1">

4816Randomized phase III trials have addressed the equivalence of substituting capecitabine for infusional 5-FU. Two phase III studies have evaluated capecitabine/oxaliplatin (CAPOX) versus 5-FU/oxaliplatin regimens (FUOX or FUFOX).[<a href="#cit/section_8.27">

481727</a>

4818,<a href="#cit/section_8.28">

481928</a>

4820]</p>

4821<p id="_946" tabindex="-1">

4822Evidence (oxaliplatin vs. capecitabine):</p>

4823<div class="pdq-content-list">

4824<ol id="_947">

4825<li>

4826The Arbeitsgemeinschaft Internische Onkologie (AIO) Colorectal Study Group randomly assigned 474 patients to either CAPOX or FUFOX. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4827<ul id="_948">

4828<li>

4829The median PFS was 7.1 months for the CAPOX arm and 8.0 months for the FUFOX arm (HR, 1.17; 95% CI, 0.96&#8211;1.43; <em>

4830P</em>

4831 = .117), and the HR was in the prespecified equivalence range.[<a href="#cit/section_8.28">

483228</a>

4833]</li>

4834</ul>

4835</div>

4836</li>

4837<li>

4838The Spanish Cooperative Group randomly assigned 348 patients to CAPOX or FUOX.[<a href="#cit/section_8.27">

483927</a>

4840][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4841Level of evidence B1</a>

4842]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4843<ul id="_949">

4844<li>

4845The TTP was 8.9 months for CAPOX versus 9.5 months for FUOX (<em>

4846P</em>

4847 = .153) and met the prespecified range for noninferiority.</li>

4848</ul>

4849</div>

4850</li>

4851</ol>

4852</div>

4853<p id="_950" tabindex="-1">

4854When using an oxaliplatin-based regimen as first-line treatment of metastatic colorectal cancer, a CAPOX regimen is not inferior to a 5-FU/oxaliplatin regimen.</p>

4855</section>

4856<section id="_951">

4857<h5 id="_951_toc">

4858Bevacizumab</h5>

4859<p id="_952" tabindex="-1">

4860 Bevacizumab can reasonably be added to either FOLFIRI or FOLFOX for patients undergoing first-line treatment of metastatic colorectal cancer. There are currently no completed randomized controlled studies evaluating whether continued use of bevacizumab in second-line or third-line treatment after progressing on a first-line bevacizumab regimen extends survival.</p>

4861<p id="_953" tabindex="-1">

4862Evidence (bevacizumab):</p>

4863<div class="pdq-content-list">

4864<ol id="_954">

4865<li>

4866After bevacizumab was approved, the BICC-C trial was amended, and an additional 117 patients were randomly assigned to receive FOLFIRI/bevacizumab or mIFL/bevacizumab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.24">

486724</a>

4868]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4869<ul id="_955">

4870<li>

4871Although the primary end point of PFS was not significantly different, patients who received FOLFIRI/bevacizumab had a significantly better OS (28.0 months vs. 19.2 months; <em>

4872P</em>

4873 = .037; HR for death, 1.79; 95% CI, 1.12&#8211;2.88). </li>

4874</ul>

4875</div>

4876</li>

4877<li>

4878In the Hurwitz study, patients with previously untreated metastatic colorectal cancer were randomly assigned to either IFL or IFL/bevacizumab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.29">

487929</a>

4880]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4881<ul id="_956">

4882<li>

4883The patients randomly assigned to the IFL/bevacizumab arm experienced a significantly better PFS (10.6 months in the IFL/bevacizumab arm compared with 6.2 months in the IFL/placebo arm; HR<sub>

4884disease progression</sub>

4885, 0.54; <em>

4886P</em>

4887 &lt; .001) and OS (20.3 months in the IFL/bevacizumab arm compared with 15.6 months in the IFL/placebo arm; HR<sub>

4888death</sub>

4889, 0.66; <em>

4890P</em>

4891 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_8.29">

489229</a>

4893]</li>

4894</ul>

4895</div>

4896</li>

4897<li>

4898Despite the lack of direct data, in standard practice bevacizumab was added to FOLFOX as a standard first-line regimen based on the results of NCCTG-N9741.[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

489921</a>

4900] Subsequently, in a randomized phase III study, 1,401 patients with untreated, stage IV colorectal cancer were randomly assigned in a 2 &#215; 2 factorial design to CAPOX versus FOLFOX4, then to bevacizumab versus placebo. PFS was the primary end point.[<a href="#cit/section_8.30">

490130</a>

4902][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4903Level of evidence B1</a>

4904] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4905<ul id="_957">

4906<li>

4907The median PFS was 9.4 months for patients who received bevacizumab and 8.0 months for the patients who received placebo (HR, 0.83; 97.5% CI, 0.72&#8211;0.95; <em>

4908P</em>

4909 = .0023).</li>

4910<li>

4911 Median OS was 21.3 months for patients who received bevacizumab and 19.9 months for patients who received placebo (HR, 0.89; 97.5% CI, 0.76&#8211;1.03; <em>

4912P</em>

4913 = .077).</li>

4914<li>

4915The median PFS (intention-to-treat analysis) was 8.0 months in the pooled CAPOX-containing arms versus 8.5 months in the FOLFOX4-containing arms (HR, 1.04; 97.5% CI, 0.93&#8211;1.16), with the upper limit of the 97.5% CI being below the predefined noninferiority margin of 1.23.[<a href="#cit/section_8.30">

491630</a>

4917,<a href="#cit/section_8.31">

491831</a>

4919]</li>

4920<li>

4921The effect of bevacizumab on OS is likely to be less than what was seen in the original Hurwitz study.</li>

4922</ul>

4923</div>

4924</li>

4925<li>

4926Investigators from the Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group randomly assigned patients who had progressed on 5-FU/LV and irinotecan to either FOLFOX or FOLFOX/bevacizumab.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4927<ul id="_958">

4928<li>

4929Patients randomly assigned to FOLFOX/bevacizumab experienced a statistically significant improvement in PFS compared with patients assigned to FOLFOX alone (7.43 months vs. 4.7 months; HR, 0.61; <em>

4930P</em>

4931 &lt; .0001) and OS (12.9 months vs. 10.8 months; HR, 0.75; <em>

4932P</em>

4933 = .0011).[<a href="#cit/section_8.32">

493432</a>

4935][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4936Level of evidence A1</a>

4937] </li>

4938</ul>

4939</div>

4940</li>

4941</ol>

4942</div>

4943</section>

4944<section id="_1115">

4945<h5 id="_1115_toc">

4946FOLFOXIRI</h5>

4947<p id="_1116" tabindex="-1">

4948Evidence (FOLFOXIRI):</p>

4949<div class="pdq-content-list">

4950<ol id="_1117">

4951<li>

4952The combination of FOLFOXIRI with bevacizumab was compared with FOLFIRI with bevacizumab in a randomized, phase III study of 508 patients with untreated metastatic colorectal cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_8.33">

495333</a>

4954]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4955<ul id="_1118">

4956<li>

4957The median PFS was 12.1 months in the FOLFOXIRI group, compared with 9.7 months in the FOLFIRI group (HR for progression, 0.75; 95% CI, 0.62&#8211;0.90; <em>

4958P</em>

4959 = .003). OS was not significantly different between the groups (31.0 vs. 25.8 months; HR<sub>

4960death</sub>

4961, 0.79; 95% CI, 0.63&#8211;1.00; <em>

4962P</em>

4963 = .054).[<a href="#cit/section_8.33">

496433</a>

4965][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4966Level of evidence B1</a>

4967] </li>

4968<li>

4969Patients who received FOLFOXIRI had significantly more grade 3 and 4 toxicities, including neutropenia, stomatitis, and peripheral neuropathy. </li>

4970</ul>

4971</div>

4972</li>

4973</ol>

4974</div>

4975</section>

4976<section id="_959">

4977<h5 id="_959_toc">

4978Cetuximab</h5>

4979<p id="_960" tabindex="-1">

4980Cetuximab is a partially humanized monoclonal antibody against EGFR. Importantly, patients with mutant <em class="gene-name">

4981KRAS</em>

4982 tumors may experience worse outcome when cetuximab is added to multiagent chemotherapy regimens containing bevacizumab.

4983

4984</p>

4985<p id="_1206" tabindex="-1">

4986Evidence (cetuximab):</p>

4987<div class="pdq-content-list">

4988<ol id="_962">

4989<li>

4990For patients who have progressed on irinotecan-containing regimens, a randomized, phase II study was performed that used either cetuximab or irinotecan/cetuximab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.34">

499134</a>

4992][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4993Level of evidence C3</a>

4994]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4995<ul id="_963">

4996<li>

4997The median TTP for patients who received cetuximab was 1.5 months, compared with median TTP of 4.2 months for patients who received irinotecan and cetuximab. On the basis of this study, cetuximab was approved for use in patients with metastatic colorectal cancer refractory to 5-FU and irinotecan.</li>

4998</ul>

4999</div>

5000</li>

5001<li>

5002The Crystal Study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00154102">

5003EMR 62202-013</a>

5004 [NCT00154102]) randomly assigned 1,198 patients with stage IV colorectal cancer to FOLFIRI with or without cetuximab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.35">

500535</a>

5006][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5007Level of evidence B1</a>

5008] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5009<ul id="_964">

5010<li>

5011The addition of cetuximab was associated with an improved PFS (HR, 0.85; 95% CI, 0.72&#8211;0.99; <em>

5012P</em>

5013 = .048 by a stratified log&#8211;rank test) but not OS.</li>

5014<li>

5015Retrospective studies of patients with metastatic colorectal cancer have suggested that responses to anti-EGFR antibody therapy are confined to patients with tumors that harbor wild types of <em class="gene-name">

5016KRAS</em>

5017 (i.e., lack activating mutations at codon 12 or 13 of the <em class="gene-name">

5018KRAS</em>

5019 gene).</li>

5020<li>

5021A subset analysis evaluating efficacy vis-&#224;-vis <em class="gene-name">

5022KRAS</em>

5023 status was done in patients enrolled in the Crystal Study. There was a significant interaction for <em class="gene-name">

5024KRAS</em>

5025 mutation status and treatment for tumor response (<em>

5026P</em>

5027 = .03) but not for PFS (<em>

5028P</em>

5029 = .07). Among patients with <em class="gene-name">

5030KRAS</em>

5031 wild-type tumors, the HR favored the FOLFIRI/cetuximab group (HR, 0.68; 95% CI, 0.50&#8211;0.94).</li>

5032</ul>

5033</div>

5034</li>

5035<li>

5036In a randomized trial, patients with metastatic colorectal cancer received capecitabine/oxaliplatin/bevacizumab with or without cetuximab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.36">

503736</a>

5038][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5039Level of evidence B1</a>

5040] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5041<ul id="_965">

5042<li>

5043The median PFS was 9.4 months in the group who received cetuximab and 10.7 months in the group who did not receive cetuximab (<em>

5044P</em>

5045 = .01).</li>

5046<li>

5047In a subset analysis, cetuximab-treated patients with tumors bearing a mutated <em class="gene-name">

5048KRAS</em>

5049 gene had significantly decreased PFS compared with cetuximab-treated patients with <em class="gene-name">

5050KRAS</em>

5051 wild-type tumors (8.1 months vs. 10.5 months; <em>

5052P</em>

5053 = .04). </li>

5054<li>

5055Cetuximab-treated patients with mutated <em class="gene-name">

5056KRAS</em>

5057 tumors had a significantly shorter PFS than patients with mutated <em class="gene-name">

5058KRAS</em>

5059 tumors who did not receive cetuximab (8.1 months vs. 12.5 months; <em>

5060P</em>

5061 = .003) and a significantly shorter OS (17.2 months vs. 24.9 months; <em>

5062P</em>

5063 = .03).</li>

5064</ul>

5065</div>

5066</li>

5067<li>

5068The Medical Research Council (MRC) (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00182715">

5069UKM-MRC-COIN-CR10</a>

5070 [NCT00182715] or COIN trial) sought to answer the question of whether adding cetuximab to combination chemotherapy with a fluoropyrimidine and oxaliplatin in first-line treatment for patients with <em class="gene-name">

5071KRAS</em>

5072 wild-type tumors was beneficial.[<a href="#cit/section_8.37">

507337</a>

5074,<a href="#cit/section_8.38">

507538</a>

5076] In addition, the MRC sought to evaluate the effect of intermittent chemotherapy versus continuous chemotherapy. The 1,630 patients were randomly assigned to three treatment groups:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5077<ul id="_1166">

5078<li>

5079Arm A: fluoropyrimidine/oxaliplatin.</li>

5080<li>

5081Arm B: fluoropyrimidine/oxaliplatin/cetuximab. </li>

5082<li>

5083Arm C: intermittent fluoropyrimidine/oxaliplatin.</li>

5084</ul>

5085</div>

5086<p id="_967" tabindex="-1">

5087The comparisons between arms A and B and arms A and C were analyzed and published separately.[<a href="#cit/section_8.37">

508837</a>

5089,<a href="#cit/section_8.38">

509038</a>

5091] </p>

5092<div class="pdq-content-list">

5093<ol id="_1200" class="lower-alpha">

5094<li>

5095In patients with <em class="gene-name">

5096KRAS</em>

5097 wild-type tumors (arm A, n = 367; arm B, n = 362), OS did not differ

5098between treatment groups (median survival, 17.9 months [interquartile range (IQR), 10.3&#8211;29.2] in the control group vs. 17.0 months [IQR, 9.4&#8211;30.1] in the cetuximab group; HR, 1.04; 95% CI, 0.87&#8211;1.23; <em>

5099P</em>

5100 = .67). Similarly, there was no effect on PFS (8.6 months [IQR, 5.0&#8211;12.5] in the control group vs. 8.6 months [IQR, 5.1&#8211;13.8] in the cetuximab group; HR, 0.96; 95% CI, 0.82&#8211;1.12, <em>

5101P </em>

5102= .60).[<a href="#cit/section_8.37">

510337</a>

5104,<a href="#cit/section_8.38">

510538</a>

5106][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5107Level of evidence A1</a>

5108] </li>

5109<li>

5110The reasons for lack of benefit in adding cetuximab are unclear. Subset analyses suggest that the use of capecitabine was associated with an inferior outcome, and the use of second-line therapy was less in patients treated with cetuximab.</li>

5111<li>

5112There was no difference between the continuously treated patients (arm A) and the intermittently treated patients (arm C). <div class="pdq-content-list">

5113<ul id="_1201">

5114<li>

5115Median survival in the intent-to-treat population (n = 815 in both groups) was 15.8 months (IQR, 9.4&#8211;26.1) in arm A and 14.4 months (IQR, 8.0&#8211;24.7) in arm C (HR, 1.084; 80% CI, 1.008&#8211;1.165).</li>

5116<li>

5117In the per-protocol population, which included only those patients who were free from progression at 12 weeks and randomly assigned to continue treatment or go on a chemotherapy holiday (arm A, n = 467; arm C, n = 511), median survival was 19.6 months (IQR, 13.0&#8211;28.1) in arm A and 18.0 months (IQR, 12.1&#8211;29.3) in arm C (HR, 1.087, 95% CI, 0.986&#8211;1.198).</li>

5118</ul>

5119</div>

5120</li>

5121<li>

5122The upper limits of CIs for HRs in both analyses were greater than the prede&#64257;ned noninferiority boundary. While intermittent chemotherapy was not deemed noninferior, there appeared to be clinically insignificant differences in patient outcomes. </li>

5123</ol>

5124</div>

5125</li>

5126</ol>

5127</div>

5128</section>

5129<section id="_1138">

5130<h5 id="_1138_toc">

5131Aflibercept</h5>

5132<p id="_1151" tabindex="-1">

5133Aflibercept is a novel anti-VEGF molecule and has been evaluated as a component of second-line therapy in patients with metastatic colorectal cancer. </p>

5134<p id="_1139" tabindex="-1">

5135Evidence (aflibercept):</p>

5136<div class="pdq-content-list">

5137<ol id="_1140">

5138<li>

5139In one trial, 1,226 patients were randomly assigned to receive aflibercept (4 mg/kg intravenously) or placebo every 2 weeks in combination with FOLFIRI.[<a href="#cit/section_8.39">

514039</a>

5141][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810019&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5142Level of evidence A2</a>

5143]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5144<ul id="_1141">

5145<li>

5146Patients who received aflibercept plus FOLFIRI had significantly improved OS rates, with median survival times of 13.50 months compared with patients who received placebo plus FOLFIRI, with median survival times of 12.06 months (HR, 0.817; 95.34% CI, 0.713&#8211;0.937; <em>

5147P</em>

5148 = .0032). </li>

5149<li>

5150Patients who received aflibercept plus FOLFIRI also had significantly improved PFS rates, with median PFS rates of 6.90 months compared with patients who received placebo plus FOLFIRI, with median PFS rates of 4.67 months (HR, 0.758; 95% CI, 0.661&#8211;0.869; <em>

5151P</em>

5152 &lt; .0001).</li>

5153<li>

5154On the basis of these results, the use of FOLFIRI plus aflibercept is an acceptable second-line regimen for patients previously treated with FOLFOX-based chemotherapy. Whether to continue bevacizumab or initiate aflibercept in second-line therapy has not been addressed as yet in any clinical trial, and there are no data available.</li>

5155</ul>

5156</div>

5157</li>

5158</ol>

5159</div>

5160</section>

5161<section id="_1195">

5162<h5 id="_1195_toc">

5163Ramucirumab</h5>

5164<p id="_1196" tabindex="-1">

5165Ramucirumab is a fully humanized monoclonal antibody that binds to vascular endothelial growth factor receptor-2 (VEGFR-2). </p>

5166<p id="_1197" tabindex="-1">

5167Evidence (ramucirumab):</p>

5168<div class="pdq-content-list">

5169<ol id="_1198">

5170<li>

5171In the randomized, unblinded, phase III <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01183780">

5172RAISE</a>

5173 study (NCT01183780), 1,072 patients with stage IV colorectal cancer who had progressed on first-line chemotherapy were randomly assigned to FOLFIRI with or without ramucirumab (8 mg/kg).[<a href="#cit/section_8.40">

517440</a>

5175][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5176Level of evidence A1</a>

5177]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5178<ul id="_1199">

5179<li>

5180 Patients assigned to FOLFIRI plus ramucirumab had a significant improvement in median OS (13.3 months vs. 11.7 months; HR, 0.84; <em>

5181P </em>

5182 = .0219) and PFS (5.7 months vs. 4.5 months; HR, 0.793; <em>

5183P</em>

5184 = .0005). </li>

5185<li>

5186 Grade 3 adverse events were more common in the ramucirumab group, including grade 3 neutropenia. </li>

5187<li>

5188 On the basis of this data, FOLFIRI plus ramucirumab is an acceptable second-line regimen for patients previously treated with FOLFOX-bevacizumab. Whether to continue bevacizumab in second-line chemotherapy or use ramucirumab in second-line chemotherapy has not yet been addressed in a clinical trial. </li>

5189</ul>

5190</div>

5191</li>

5192</ol>

5193</div>

5194</section>

5195<section id="_969">

5196<h5 id="_969_toc">

5197Panitumumab</h5>

5198<p id="_970" tabindex="-1">

5199Panitumumab is a fully humanized antibody against the EGFR. The FDA approved panitumumab for use in patients with metastatic colorectal cancer refractory to chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.41">

520041</a>

5201] In clinical trials, panitumumab demonstrated efficacy as a single agent or in combination therapy, which was consistent with the effects on PFS and OS with cetuximab. There appears to be a consistent class effect.</p>

5202<p id="_971" tabindex="-1">

5203Evidence (panitumumab):</p>

5204<div class="pdq-content-list">

5205<ol id="_972">

5206<li>

5207 In a phase III trial, patients with chemotherapy-refractory colorectal cancer were randomly assigned to panitumumab or best supportive care.[<a href="#cit/section_8.41">

520841</a>

5209][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5210Level of evidence B1</a>

5211]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5212<ul id="_1113">

5213<li>

5214Patients who received panitumumab experienced an improved PFS (8 weeks vs. 7.3 weeks; HR, 0.54; 95% CI, 0.44&#8211;0.66; <em>

5215P</em>

5216 &lt; .0001).</li>

5217<li>

5218There was no difference in OS, which was thought to be the result of 76% of patients on best supportive care crossing over to panitumumab.</li>

5219</ul>

5220</div>

5221</li>

5222<li>

5223In the Panitumumab Randomized Trial in Combination With Chemotherapy for

5224Metastatic Colorectal Cancer to Determine Efficacy (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00364013">

5225PRIME</a>

5226 [NCT00364013]) study, 1,183 patients were randomly assigned to FOLFOX4 with or without panitumumab as first-line therapy for metastatic colorectal cancer. The study was amended to enlarge the sample size to address patients with <em class="gene-name">

5227KRAS</em>

5228 wild-type tumors and patients with mutant <em class="gene-name">

5229KRAS</em>

5230 tumors separately.[<a href="#cit/section_8.42">

523142</a>

5232][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5233Level of evidence B1</a>

5234] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5235<ol id="_1106" class="lower-alpha">

5236<li>

5237For patients with <em class="gene-name">

5238KRAS</em>

5239 wild-type tumors, a statistically significant improvement in PFS was observed in those who received panitumumab/FOLFOX4 compared with those who received only FOLFOX4 (HR, 0.80; 95% CI, 0.66&#8211;0.97; <em>

5240P</em>

5241 = .02, stratified log-rank test).</li>

5242<li>

5243Median PFS was 9.6 months (95% CI, 9.2&#8211;11.1 months) for patients who received panitumumab/FOLFOX4 and 8.0 months (95% CI, 7.5&#8211;9.3 months) for patients who received FOLFOX4. OS was not significantly different between the groups (HR, 0.83; 95% CI, 0.67&#8211;1.02; <em>

5244P</em>

5245 = .072).</li>

5246<li>

5247For patients with mutant <em class="gene-name">

5248KRAS</em>

5249 tumors, PFS was worse with the addition of panitumumab (HR, 1.29; 95% CI, 1.04&#8211;1.62; <em>

5250P</em>

5251 = .02, stratified log&#8211;rank test). <div class="pdq-content-list">

5252<ul id="_974">

5253<li>

5254Median PFS was 7.3 months (95% CI, 6.3&#8211;8.0 months) for panitumumab/FOLFOX4 and 8.8 months (95% CI, 7.7&#8211;9.4 months) for FOLFOX4 alone.</li>

5255</ul>

5256</div>

5257</li>

5258<li>

5259Subsequently, a retrospective analysis evaluated patients with wild-type <em class="gene-name">

5260KRAS</em>

5261 exon 2 wild-type status for other <em class="gene-name">

5262KRAS</em>

5263 and <em class="gene-name">

5264BRAF</em>

5265 mutations.[<a href="#cit/section_8.43">

526643</a>

5267][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5268Level of evidence C1</a>

5269]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5270<ul id="_1211">

5271<li>

5272Of the 620 patients who were initially identified as not having a mutation in exon 2 of <em class="gene-name">

5273KRAS</em>

5274, 108 patients (17%) were found to have additional <em class="gene-name">

5275RAS</em>

5276 mutations and 53 patients (8%) were found to have <em class="gene-name">

5277BRAF</em>

5278 mutations. In a retrospective analysis, patients without any <em class="gene-name">

5279RAS</em>

5280 or <em class="gene-name">

5281BRAF</em>

5282 mutations had a longer PFS (10.8 months vs. 9.2 months, <em>

5283P</em>

5284 = .002) and OS (28.3 months vs. 20.9 months, <em>

5285P</em>

5286 = .02) when assigned to the FOLFOX4/panitumumab arm than the patients assigned to the FOLFOX4 arm.</li>

5287</ul>

5288</div>

5289</li>

5290</ol>

5291</div>

5292</li>

5293<li>

5294Similarly, the addition of panitumumab to a regimen of FOLFOX/bevacizumab resulted in a worse PFS and worse toxicity compared with a regimen of FOLFOX/bevacizumab alone in patients not selected for <em class="gene-name">

5295KRAS</em>

5296 mutation in metastatic rectal cancer (11.4 months vs. 10.0 months; HR, 1.27; 95% CI, 1.06&#8211;1.52).[<a href="#cit/section_8.44">

529744</a>

5298][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5299Level of evidence B1</a>

5300]</li>

5301<li>

5302In another study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00339183">

5303NCT00339183</a>

5304), patients with metastatic colorectal cancer who had already received a fluoropyrimidine regimen were randomly assigned to either FOLFIRI or FOLFIRI/panitumumab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.45">

530545</a>

5306][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5307Level of evidence B1</a>

5308]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5309<ol id="_1107" class="lower-alpha">

5310<li>

5311In a post hoc analysis, patients with <em class="gene-name">

5312KRAS</em>

5313 wild-type tumors experienced a statistically significant PFS advantage (HR, 0.73; 95% CI, 0.59&#8211;0.90; <em>

5314P</em>

5315 = .004, stratified log-rank).<div class="pdq-content-list">

5316<ul id="_976">

5317<li>

5318Median PFS was 5.9 months (95% CI, 5.5&#8211;6.7 months) for FOLFIRI/panitumumab and 3.9 months (95% CI, 3.7&#8211;5.3 months) for FOLFIRI alone.</li>

5319</ul>

5320</div>

5321</li>

5322<li>

5323OS was not significantly different. Median OS was 14.5 months for the FOLFIRI/panitumumab group versus 12.5 months for the FOLFIRI alone group.</li>

5324<li>

5325Patients with mutant <em class="gene-name">

5326KRAS</em>

5327 tumors experienced no benefit from the addition of panitumumab.</li>

5328</ol>

5329</div>

5330</li>

5331</ol>

5332</div>

5333</section>

5334<section id="_1127">

5335<h5 id="_1127_toc">

5336Anti-EGFR antibody versus anti-VEGF antibody with first-line chemotherapy</h5>

5337<p id="_1128" tabindex="-1">

5338In the management of patients with stage IV colorectal cancer, it is unknown whether patients with <em class="gene-name">

5339KRAS</em>

5340 wild-type cancer should receive an anti-EGFR antibody with chemotherapy or an anti-VEGF antibody with chemotherapy. Two studies attempted to answer this question.[<a href="#cit/section_8.46">

534146</a>

5342,<a href="#cit/section_8.47">

534347</a>

5344]</p>

5345<p id="_1174" tabindex="-1">

5346Evidence (anti-EGFR antibody vs. anti-VEGF antibody with first-line chemotherapy): </p>

5347<div class="pdq-content-list">

5348<ol id="_1129">

5349<li>

5350The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00433927">

5351FIRE-3</a>

5352 study (NCT00433927) randomly assigned 592 patients with <em class="gene-name">

5353KRAS</em>

5354 exon 2 wild-type tumors who were previously untreated to FOLFIRI plus cetuximab (297 patients) or FOLFIRI plus bevacizumab (295 patients). The primary end point of the study was objective response rate.[<a href="#cit/section_8.46">

535546</a>

5356][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5357Level of evidence A1</a>

5358] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5359<ul id="_1130">

5360<li>

5361The objective response rate was not significantly different between the groups (objective response rate, 62.0%; 95% CI, 56.2&#8211;67.5 vs. objective response rate, 58.0%; 95% CI, 52.1&#8211;63.7; odds ratio, 1.18; 95% CI, 0.85&#8211;1.64; <em>

5362P</em>

5363 = .18). </li>

5364<li>

5365Median PFS was 10.0 months (95% CI, 8.8&#8211;10.8) in the cetuximab group and 10.3 months (95% CI, 9.8&#8211;11.3) in the bevacizumab group (HR, 1.06; 95% CI, 0.88&#8211;1.26; <em>

5366P</em>

5367 = .55). </li>

5368<li>

5369Median OS was 28.7 months (95% CI, 24.0&#8211;36.6) in the cetuximab group compared with 25.0 months (range, 22.7&#8211;27.6 months) in the bevacizumab group (HR, 0.77; 95% CI, 0.62&#8211;0.96; <em>

5370P</em>

5371 = .017). </li>

5372<li>

5373 In a post hoc analysis of patients with expanded <em class="gene-name">

5374RAS</em>

5375 wild-type tumors (sequencing for mutational hot spots within <em class="gene-name">

5376KRAS</em>

5377 and <em class="gene-name">

5378NRAS</em>

5379 genes, including exon 2 codons 12 and 13; exon 3 codons 59 and 61; and exon 4 codons 117 and 146), the median OS was 33.1 months (95% CI, 24.5&#8211;39.4) in the cetuximab group compared with 25.0 months (95% CI, 23.0&#8211;28.1) in the bevacizumab group (HR, 0.70; 95% CI, 0.54&#8211;0.90; <em>

5380P</em>

5381 = .0059).[<a href="#cit/section_8.48">

538248</a>

5383]</li>

5384<li>

5385Of note, only 52% of patients assigned to the bevacizumab arm subsequently received cetuximab or panitumumab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.49">

538649</a>

5387] </li>

5388</ul>

5389</div>

5390</li>

5391<li>

5392The Cancer and Leukemia Group B <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00265850">

5393Intergroup study 80405</a>

5394 (NCT00265850) was presented at the American Society of Clinical Oncology meeting in 2014. This study randomly assigned 2,334 previously untreated patients with <em class="gene-name">

5395KRAS</em>

5396 wild-type cancer to chemotherapy (FOLFOX or FOLFIRI) plus bevacizumab or chemotherapy plus cetuximab. OS was the primary end point.[<a href="#cit/section_8.47">

539747</a>

5398][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5399Level of evidence B1</a>

5400] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5401<ul id="_1131">

5402<li>

5403There was no statistically significant difference in OS among the patients assigned to bevacizumab or cetuximab (for OS differences, chemotherapy/bevacizumab = 29.04 months [range, 25.66&#8211;31.21 months] vs. chemotherapy/cetuximab = 29.93 months [range, 27.56&#8211;31.21 months]; HR, 0.92 [0.78&#8211;1.09]; <em>

5404P</em>

5405 = .34). </li>

5406</ul>

5407</div>

5408 </li>

5409</ol>

5410</div>

5411<p id="_1132" tabindex="-1">

5412On the basis of these two studies, no apparent significant difference is evident about starting treatment with chemotherapy/bevacizumab or chemotherapy/cetuximab in patients with <em class="gene-name">

5413KRAS</em>

5414 wild-type metastatic colorectal cancer. However, in patients with <em class="gene-name">

5415KRAS</em>

5416 wild-type cancer, administration of an anti-EGFR antibody at some point in the course of management improves OS.

5417

5418</p>

5419</section>

5420<section id="_1142">

5421<h5 id="_1142_toc">

5422Regorafenib</h5>

5423<p id="_1152" tabindex="-1">

5424Regorafenib is an inhibitor of multiple tyrosine kinase pathways including VEGF. In September 2012, the FDA <a href="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2017/203085s007lbl.pdf" title="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2017/203085s007lbl.pdf">

5425granted approval</a>

5426 for the use of regorafenib in patients who had progressed on previous therapy. </p>

5427<p id="_1143" tabindex="-1">

5428Evidence (regorafenib):</p>

5429<div class="pdq-content-list">

5430<ol id="_1144">

5431<li>

5432The safety and effectiveness of regorafenib were evaluated in a single, clinical study of 760 patients with previously treated metastatic colorectal cancer. Patients were randomly assigned in a 2:1 fashion to receive regorafenib or a placebo in addition to the best supportive care.[<a href="#cit/section_8.50">

543350</a>

5434,<a href="#cit/section_8.51">

543551</a>

5436] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5437<ul id="_1145">

5438<li>

5439Patients treated with regorafenib had a statistically significant improvement in OS (6.4 months in the regorafenib group vs. 5.0 months in the placebo group; HR, 0.77; 95% CI, 0.64&#8211;0.94; one-sided <em>

5440P</em>

5441 = .0052).</li>

5442</ul>

5443</div>

5444</li>

5445</ol>

5446</div>

5447</section>

5448<section id="_1146">

5449<h5 id="_1146_toc">

5450TAS-102</h5>

5451<p id="_1147" tabindex="-1">

5452TAS-102 (<a href="https://www.taihooncology.com/us/prescribing-information.pdf" title="https://www.taihooncology.com/us/prescribing-information.pdf">

5453Lonsurf</a>

5454) is an orally administered combination of a thymidine-based nucleic acid analog, trifluridine, and a thymidine phosphorylase inhibitor, tipiracil hydrochloride. Trifluridine, in its triphosphate form, inhibits thymidylate synthase; therefore, trifluridine, in this form, has an anti-tumor effect. Tipiracil hydrochloride is a potent inhibitor of thymidine phosphorylase, which actively degrades trifluridine. The combination of trifluridine and tipiracil allows for adequate plasma levels of trifluridine.</p>

5455<p id="_1148" tabindex="-1">

5456Evidence (TAS-102):</p>

5457<div class="pdq-content-list">

5458<ol id="_1149">

5459<li>

5460A phase III, double-blind study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01607957">

5461RECOURSE</a>

5462 [NCT01607957]) randomly assigned 800 stage IV colorectal cancer patients whose cancer had been refractory to two previous therapies. Patients were required to have received 5-FU, oxaliplatin, irinotecan, bevacizumab and, if the patients had <em class="gene-name">

5463KRAS</em>

5464 wild-type cancer, cetuximab or panitumumab. Patients were randomly assigned in a 2:1 ratio to receive best supportive care plus TAS-102 (n = 534) or placebo (n = 266). The median age of patients was 63 years, and the majority of patients (60%&#8211;63%) had received four or more previous lines of therapy. All patients had formerly received fluoropyrimidine, irinotecan, oxaliplatin, and bevacizumab, and 52% of them had received an EGFR inhibitor. Approximately 20% of the patients had received previous treatment with regorafenib.[<a href="#cit/section_8.52">

546552</a>

5466][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5467Level of evidence A1</a>

5468] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5469<ul id="_1150">

5470<li>

5471TAS-102 was administered at 35 mg/m<span class="sup">

54722</span>

5473 twice daily with meals for 5 days, with 2 days of rest for 2 weeks, followed by a 14-day rest period. </li>

5474<li>

5475The primary end point of the study was OS. The median OS for patients with metastatic colorectal cancer who received TAS-102 was 7.1 months compared with 5.3 months for those who received a placebo (HR, 0.68; <em>

5476P</em>

5477 &lt; .0001). </li>

5478<li>

5479The median PFS time in the TAS-102 arm was 2 months versus 1.7 months with a placebo (HR, 0.48; <em>

5480P</em>

5481 &lt; .0001).</li>

5482<li>

5483Secondary end points focused on PFS, overall response rate, and disease control rate.</li>

5484<li>

5485The overall response rate was 1.6% with TAS-102, which consisted of a complete response in one patient and partial responses in other patients. The overall response rate with a placebo was 0.4% (<em>

5486P</em>

5487 = .29). </li>

5488</ul>

5489</div>

5490</li>

5491</ol>

5492</div>

5493<p id="_1153" tabindex="-1">

5494The FDA approved TAS-102 for the treatment of metastatic colorectal cancer patients on the basis of the results of the RECOURSE trial.</p>

5495</section>

5496<section id="_1267">

5497<h5 id="_1267_toc">

5498Encorafenib with cetuximab for patients with <em class="gene-name">

5499BRAF</em>

5500 V600E mutations</h5>

5501<p id="_1268" tabindex="-1">

5502<em class="gene-name">

5503BRAF</em>

5504 V600E mutations occur in about 10% of metastatic colorectal cancers and are an indicator of poor prognosis. Unlike in melanoma, BRAF inhibitor monotherapy has not shown a benefit in colorectal cancer, and multiple studies have evaluated concurrent targeting of the EGFR-MAPK pathway.</p>

5505<p id="_1269" tabindex="-1">

5506Evidence (encorafenib with cetuximab for patients with <em class="gene-name">

5507BRAF</em>

5508 V600E mutations):</p>

5509<div class="pdq-content-list">

5510<ol id="_1270">

5511<li>

5512Encorafenib (BRAF inhibitor), binimetinib (MEK inhibitor), and cetuximab (EGFR inhibitor):

5513In the international, open-label, randomized, phase III <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02928224">

5514BEACON</a>

5515 trial, patients with metastatic colorectal cancer and <em class="gene-name">

5516BRAF</em>

5517 V600E mutations who previously received one or two treatment regimens were enrolled.[<a href="#cit/section_8.53">

551853</a>

5519] The trial randomly assigned 665 patients in a 1:1:1 ratio to receive one of the following:

5520<div class="pdq-content-list">

5521<ul id="_1271">

5522<li>

5523 Triplet therapy: encorafenib (300 mg PO daily), binimetinib (45 mg PO twice daily), and cetuximab (400 mg/m<span class="sup">

55242</span>

5525 IV loading dose followed by 250 mg/m<span class="sup">

55262</span>

5527 IV weekly) (n = 224).</li>

5528<li>

5529 Doublet therapy: encorafenib and cetuximab (as per triplet therapy dosing) (n = 220). </li>

5530<li>

5531 Control group: FOLFIRI or irinotecan (every 2 weeks) with cetuximab (400 mg/m<span class="sup">

55322</span>

5533 IV loading dose followed by 250 mg/m<span class="sup">

55342</span>

5535 IV weekly) (n = 221). </li>

5536</ul>

5537</div>

5538The primary end points were OS and objective response in the triplet-therapy group when compared with the control group.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5539<ul id="_1272">

5540<li>

5541 The OS was 9.0 months in the triplet-therapy arm and 5.4 months in the control group (HR, 0.52; 95% CI, 0.39&#8211;0.70, <em>

5542P</em>

5543 &lt; .0001).[<a href="#cit/section_8.53">

554453</a>

5545][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5546Level of evidence A1</a>

5547]</li>

5548<li>

5549 Grade 3 or higher side effects occurred in 58% of patients in the triplet-therapy arm, with 10% of patients experiencing diarrhea and 11% of patients experiencing anemia. Grade 3 or higher side effects occurred in 50% of patients in the doublet-therapy arm and 61% of patients in the control arm. Fourteen percent of patients who received the doublet regimen developed melanocytic nevi.</li>

5550</ul>

5551</div>

5552Updated data were presented in abstract form in May 2020:[<a href="#cit/section_8.54">

555354</a>

5554]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5555<ul id="_1273">

5556<li>

5557The median OS was 9.3 months in both the triplet-therapy and doublet-therapy arms and 5.9 months in the control arm (HR, 0.60 for triplet therapy vs. control; 95% CI, 0.47&#8211;0.75; HR, 0.61 for doublet therapy vs. control; 95% CI, 0.48&#8211;0.77). </li>

5558<li>

5559The objective response rate was 26.8% for patients who received triplet therapy (95% CI, 21.1%&#8211;33.1%) and 19.5% for patients who received doublet therapy (95% CI, 14.5%&#8211;25.4%).</li>

5560</ul>

5561</div>

5562</li>

5563</ol>

5564</div>

5565<p id="_1274" tabindex="-1">

5566Based on these data, the FDA approved the combination of encorafenib with cetuximab for patients with previously treated <em class="gene-name">

5567BRAF</em>

5568 V600E-mutated metastatic colorectal cancer in April 2020.</p>

5569</section>

5570</section>

5571<section id="_1275">

5572<h4 id="_1275_toc">

5573Second-line chemotherapy</h4>

5574<p id="_1276" tabindex="-1">

5575Second-line chemotherapy with irinotecan in patients treated with 5-FU/LV as first-line therapy demonstrated improved OS when compared with either infusional 5-FU or supportive care.[<a href="#cit/section_8.55">

557655</a>

5577-<a href="#cit/section_8.58">

557858</a>

5579]</p>

5580<p id="_1277" tabindex="-1">

5581Similarly, a phase III trial randomly assigned patients who progressed on irinotecan and 5-FU/LV to bolus and infusional 5-FU/LV, single-agent oxaliplatin, or FOLFOX4. The median TTP for FOLFOX4 versus 5-FU/LV was 4.6 months versus 2.7 months (stratified log-rank test, 2-sided <em>

5582P</em>

5583 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_8.59">

558459</a>

5585][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5586Level of evidence B1</a>

5587]</p>

5588</section>

5589<section id="_1278">

5590<h4 id="_1278_toc">

5591Immunotherapy</h4>

5592<p id="_1279" tabindex="-1">

5593Approximately 4% of patients with stage IV colorectal cancer have tumors that are mismatch repair deficient (dMMR) or microsatellite unstable/microsatellite instability-high (MSI-H). The MSI-H phenotype is associated with germline defects in the <em class="gene-name">

5594MLH1</em>

5595, <em class="gene-name">

5596MSH2</em>

5597, <em class="gene-name">

5598MSH6</em>

5599, and <em class="gene-name">

5600PMS2</em>

5601 genes and is the primary phenotype observed in tumors from patients with hereditary nonpolyposis colorectal cancer (HNPCC) or Lynch syndrome. Patients can also have the MSI-H phenotype because one of these genes was silenced via DNA methylation. Testing for microsatellite instability can be done with molecular genetic tests, which look for microsatellite instability in the tumor tissue, or with immunohistochemistry, which looks for the loss of mismatch repair proteins. MSI-H status has historically been prognostic of increased survival for patients with earlier-stage disease and since 2015, has also been found to predict tumor response to checkpoint inhibition. </p>

5602<p id="_1280" tabindex="-1">

5603The FDA approved pembrolizumab for use in patients with treatment-na&#239;ve, metastatic, dMMR/MSI-H colorectal cancer in June 2020. Studies regarding first-line treatment with dual checkpoint inhibitors are ongoing. The FDA approved the anti-programmed cell death protein 1 (PD-1) antibodies pembrolizumab in May 2017 and nivolumab in July 2017 for the treatment of patients with microsatellite-unstable tumors who had previously received 5-FU, oxaliplatin, and irinotecan-based therapy. In July 2018, the FDA granted accelerated approval for the combination of nivolumab with ipilimumab (a CTLA-4 inhibitor) to treat MSI-H colorectal cancers that progressed after prior 5-FU, oxaliplatin, and irinotecan-based therapies.</p>

5604<section id="_1281">

5605<h5 id="_1281_toc">

5606First-line immunotherapy</h5>

5607<section id="_1282">

5608<h6 id="_1282_toc">

5609Pembrolizumab monotherapy</h6>

5610<p id="_1283" tabindex="-1">

5611Evidence (pembrolizumab monotherapy):</p>

5612<div class="pdq-content-list">

5613<ol id="_1284">

5614<li>

5615In the phase III, open-label, international, randomized <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02563002">

5616KEYNOTE-177</a>

5617 trial (NCT02563002), 307 patients with treatment-na&#239;ve MSI-H or dMMR metastatic colorectal cancer were randomly assigned in a 1:1 ratio to receive either pembrolizumab (200 mg every 3 weeks) or chemotherapy (FOLFIRI or modified FOLFOX-6 with or without bevacizumab or cetuximab).[<a href="#cit/section_8.60">

561860</a>

5619]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5620<ul id="_1285">

5621<li>

5622The median PFS was 16.5 months for patients who received pembrolizumab and 8.2 months for patients who received chemotherapy (HR, 0.60; 95% CI, 0.45&#8211;0.80; <em>

5623P</em>

5624 = .0002).[<a href="#cit/section_8.60">

562560</a>

5626][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810021&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810021&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5627Level of evidence A3</a>

5628]</li>

5629<li>

5630The PFS in prespecified subgroups showed HRs that favored the pembrolizumab arm, except in patients with <em class="gene-name">

5631KRAS</em>

5632 or <em class="gene-name">

5633NRAS</em>

5634 mutations.</li>

5635<li>

5636The objective response rate was 43.8% in the pembrolizumab arm and 33.3% in the chemotherapy arm. The median duration of response was not reached in the pembrolizumab arm (range, 2.3&#8211;41.4 months) and was 10.6 months in the chemotherapy arm (range, 2.8&#8211;37.5 months).</li>

5637<li>

5638 Grade 3 or higher adverse events occurred in 56% of patients who received pembrolizumab (with 9% experiencing grade 3 or higher infusion-related adverse events), compared with 78% of patients who received chemotherapy.</li>

5639<li>

5640 A final review of OS, presented in abstract form, showed that median OS was not reached in the pembrolizumab arm and was 36.7 months in the chemotherapy arm (HR, 0.74; 95% CI, 0.53&#8211;1.03; <em>

5641P</em>

5642 = .0359).[<a href="#cit/section_8.61">

564361</a>

5644]</li>

5645</ul>

5646</div>

5647</li>

5648</ol>

5649</div>

5650</section>

5651<section id="_1286">

5652<h6 id="_1286_toc">

5653Nivolumab and ipilimumab</h6>

5654<p id="_1287" tabindex="-1">

5655Evidence (nivolumab and ipilimumab):</p>

5656<div class="pdq-content-list">

5657<ol id="_1288">

5658<li>

5659In a single-arm cohort of the phase II, multicenter <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02060188">

5660CheckMate-142</a>

5661 study (NCT02060188) presented in abstract form, 45 treatment-na&#239;ve patients with MSI-H/dMMR metastatic colorectal cancer received nivolumab (3 mg/kg every 2 weeks) with ipilimumab (1 mg/kg every 6 weeks). The primary end point was objective response rate.[<a href="#cit/section_8.62">

566262</a>

5663]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5664<ul id="_1289">

5665<li>

5666 The objective response rate was 69% among all enrolled patients and 80% for patients with <em class="gene-name">

5667KRAS</em>

5668 mutations (n = 10).[<a href="#cit/section_8.62">

566962</a>

5670][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5671Level of evidence C2</a>

5672]</li>

5675</ul>

5677</li>

5680</section>

5681</section>

5682<section id="_1290">

5683<h5 id="_1290_toc">

5684Second-line immunotherapy</h5>

5685<section id="_1291">

5686<h6 id="_1291_toc">

5687Pembrolizumab monotherapy</h6>

5688<p id="_1292" tabindex="-1">

5689Evidence (pembrolizumab monotherapy):</p>

5690<div class="pdq-content-list">

5691<ol id="_1293">

5692<li>

5693The FDA approval of pembrolizumab monotherapy was based on data from 149 patients with MSI-H or dMMR cancers enrolled across five uncontrolled, multicohort, multicenter, single-arm clinical trials. Ninety patients had colorectal cancer, and 59 patients were diagnosed with 1 of 14 other cancer types. Patients received either 200 mg of pembrolizumab every 3 weeks or 10 mg/kg of pembrolizumab every 2 weeks. Treatment continued until unacceptable toxicity or disease progression occurred. The major efficacy outcome measures were objective response rate (assessed by blinded independent central radiologists&#8217; review in accordance with Response Evaluation Criteria in Solid Tumors [RECIST] 1.1) and response duration.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5694<ul id="_1294">

5695<li>

5696The objective response rate was 39.6% (95% CI, 31.7%&#8211;47.9%). </li>

5697<li>

5698Responses lasted 6 months or longer for 78% of patients who responded to pembrolizumab. There were 11 complete responses and 48 partial responses. </li>

5699<li>

5700The objective response rate was similar whether patients were diagnosed with colorectal cancer (36%) or a different cancer (46% across the 14 other cancer types).</li>

5701</ul>

5702</div>

5703</li>

5704</ol>

5705</div>

5706</section>

5707<section id="_1295">

5708<h6 id="_1295_toc">

5709Nivolumab monotherapy</h6>

5710<p id="_1296" tabindex="-1">

5711Evidence (nivolumab monotherapy):</p>

5712<div class="pdq-content-list">

5713<ol id="_1297">

5714<li>

5715In the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02060188">

5716CheckMate-142</a>

5717 trial (NCT02060188), 74 patients with previously treated dMMR/MSI-H colorectal cancer were enrolled in an open-label, single-arm, phase II study to receive nivolumab (3 mg/kg every 2 weeks). The primary end point was objective response as per RECIST 1.1.[<a href="#cit/section_8.63">

571863</a>

5719]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5720<ul id="_1298">

5721<li>

5722 The objective response rate was 31.1% (95% CI, 20.8%&#8211;42.9%).</li>

5723<li>

5724 Grade 3 to 4 treatment-related adverse events occurred in 21% of patients. </li>

5725</ul>

5726</div>

5727</li>

5728</ol>

5729</div>

5730</section>

5731<section id="_1299">

5732<h6 id="_1299_toc">

5733Nivolumab and ipilimumab</h6>

5734<p id="_1300" tabindex="-1">

5735Evidence (nivolumab and ipilimumab):</p>

5736<div class="pdq-content-list">

5737<ol id="_1301">

5738<li>

5739<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02060188">

5740CheckMate-142</a>

5741 (NCT02060188) was a multicenter, open-label, phase II trial with a cohort for patients with recurrent or metastatic dMMR and/or MSI-H colorectal cancer who had progressed on, were intolerant of, or declined at least one line of chemotherapy (including 5-FU and oxaliplatin and/or irinotecan). The trial enrolled 119 patients who received four doses of nivolumab (3 mg/kg) and ipilimumab (1 mg/kg) every 3 weeks (induction), then nivolumab (3 mg/kg IV) every 2 weeks (maintenance). The primary end point was objective response rate.[<a href="#cit/section_8.63">

574263</a>

5743]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5744<ul id="_1302">

5745<li>

5746 The objective response rate was 55% (95% CI, 45.2%&#8211;63.8%).</li>

5747<li>

5748 Among patients experiencing a response, 83% had responses lasting more than 6 months.</li>

5749<li>

5750 Grade 3 to 4 treatment-related adverse events occurred in 32% of patients.</li>

5751</ul>

5752</div>

5753</li>

5754</ol>

5755</div>

5756</section>

5757</section>

5758</section>

5759<section id="_980">

5760<h4 id="_980_toc">

5761Palliative therapy</h4>

5762<p id="_981" tabindex="-1">

5763Palliative radiation therapy,[<a href="#cit/section_8.11">

576411</a>

5765,<a href="#cit/section_8.58">

576658</a>

5767] chemotherapy,[<a href="#cit/section_8.13">

576813</a>

5769,<a href="#cit/section_8.64">

577064</a>

5771-<a href="#cit/section_8.69">

577269</a>

5773] and chemoradiation therapy [<a href="#cit/section_8.70">

577470</a>

5775,<a href="#cit/section_8.71">

577671</a>

5777] may be indicated. Palliative, endoscopically-placed stents may be used to relieve obstruction.[<a href="#cit/section_8.72">

577872</a>

5779]</p>

5780</section>

5781</section>

5782<section id="_982">

5783<h3 id="_982_toc">

5784Treatment of Liver Metastasis</h3>

5785<p id="_983" tabindex="-1">

5786Approximately 15% to 25% of colorectal cancer patients will present with liver metastases at diagnosis, and another 25% to 50% will develop metachronous hepatic metastasis after resection of the primary tumor.[<a href="#cit/section_8.73">

578773</a>

5788-<a href="#cit/section_8.75">

578975</a>

5790] Although only a small proportion of patients with liver metastasis are candidates for surgical resection, advances in tumor ablation techniques and in both regional and systemic chemotherapy administration provide a number of treatment options. These include the following:</p>

5791<div class="pdq-content-list">

5792<ol id="_984">

5793<li>

5794<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_985">

5795Surgery</a>

5796.</li>

5797<li>

5798<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_989">

5799Neoadjuvant chemotherapy</a>

5800.</li>

5801<li>

5802<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_991">

5803Local ablation</a>

5804.</li>

5805<li>

5806<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_994">

5807Adjuvant chemotherapy</a>

5808.</li>

5809<li>

5810<a href="/types/colorectal/hp/rectal-treatment-pdq#_1001">

5811Intra-arterial chemotherapy after liver resection</a>

5812.</li>

5813</ol>

5814</div>

5815<section id="_985">

5816<h4 id="_985_toc">

5817Surgery</h4>

5818<p id="_986" tabindex="-1">

5819Hepatic metastasis may be considered resectable on the basis of the following factors:[<a href="#cit/section_8.57">

582057</a>

5821,<a href="#cit/section_8.76">

582276</a>

5823-<a href="#cit/section_8.88">

582488</a>

5825]</p>

5826<div class="pdq-content-list">

5827<ul id="_987">

5828<li>

5829Limited number of lesions.</li>

5830<li>

5831Intrahepatic locations of lesions.</li>

5832<li>

5833Lack of major vascular involvement.</li>

5834<li>

5835Absent or limited extrahepatic disease.</li>

5836<li>

5837Sufficient functional hepatic reserve.</li>

5838</ul>

5839</div>

5840<p id="_988" tabindex="-1">

5841For patients with hepatic metastasis that is considered resectable, a negative margin resection has been associated with 5-year survival rates of 25% to 40% in mostly nonrandomized studies, such as the North Central Cancer Treatment Group trial <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00002575">

5842NCCTG-934653</a>

5843 (NCT00002575).[<a href="#cit/section_8.89">

584489</a>

5845-<a href="#cit/section_8.93">

584693</a>

5847][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5848Level of evidence C3</a>

5849] Improved surgical techniques and advances in preoperative imaging have improved patient selection for resection. In addition, multiple studies with multiagent chemotherapy have demonstrated that patients with metastatic disease isolated to the liver, which historically would be considered unresectable, can occasionally be made resectable after the administration of neoadjuvant chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.94">

585094</a>

5851]</p>

5852</section>

5853<section id="_989">

5854<h4 id="_989_toc">

5855Neoadjuvant chemotherapy </h4>

5856<p id="_990" tabindex="-1">

5857Patients with hepatic metastases that are deemed unresectable will occasionally become candidates for resection if they have a good response to chemotherapy. These patients have 5-year survival rates similar to patients who initially had resectable disease.[<a href="#cit/section_8.94">

585894</a>

5859]</p>

5860</section>

5861<section id="_991">

5862<h4 id="_991_toc">

5863Local ablation</h4>

5864<p id="_992" tabindex="-1">

5865Radiofrequency ablation has emerged as a safe technique (2% major morbidity and &lt;1% mortality rate) that may provide long-term tumor control.[<a href="#cit/section_8.95">

586695</a>

5867-<a href="#cit/section_8.101">

5868101</a>

5869] Radiofrequency ablation and cryosurgical ablation remain options for patients with tumors that cannot be resected and for patients who are not candidates for liver resection. </p>

5870</section>

5871<section id="_994">

5872<h4 id="_994_toc">

5873Adjuvant chemotherapy</h4>

5874<p id="_995" tabindex="-1">

5875The role of adjuvant chemotherapy after potentially curative resection of liver metastases is uncertain.</p>

5876<p id="_996" tabindex="-1">

5877Evidence (adjuvant chemotherapy):</p>

5878<div class="pdq-content-list">

5879<ol id="_997">

5880<li>

5881A trial of hepatic arterial floxuridine and dexamethasone plus systemic 5-FU/LV compared with systemic 5-FU/LV alone showed improved 2-year PFS (57% vs. 42%; <em>

5882P</em>

5883 =.07) and OS (86% vs. 72%; <em>

5884P</em>

5885 = .03) for patients in the combined therapy arm but did not show a significant statistical difference in

5886median survival when compared with systemic 5-FU therapy alone.[<a href="#cit/section_8.102">

5887102</a>

5888][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5889Level of evidence A1</a>

5890] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5891<ul id="_998">

5892<li>

5893Median survival in the combined therapy arm was 72.2 months versus 59.3 months in the monotherapy arm (<em>

5894P</em>

5895 = .21).</li>

5896</ul>

5897</div>

5898</li>

5899<li>

5900A second trial preoperatively randomly assigned patients with one to three potentially resectable colorectal hepatic metastases to either no further therapy or postoperative hepatic arterial floxuridine plus systemic 5-FU.[<a href="#cit/section_8.103">

5901103</a>

5902] Among those randomly assigned patients, 27% were deemed ineligible at the time of surgery, leaving only 75 patients evaluable for recurrence and survival.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5903<ul id="_999">

5904<li>

5905While liver recurrence was decreased, median or 4-year survival was not significantly different between the patient groups.</li>

5906</ul>

5907</div>

5908</li>

5909</ol>

5910</div>

5911<p id="_1000" tabindex="-1">

5912Additional studies are required to evaluate this treatment approach and to determine whether more effective systemic combination chemotherapy alone would provide results similar to hepatic intra-arterial therapy plus systemic treatment.</p>

5913</section>

5914<section id="_1001">

5915<h4 id="_1001_toc">

5916Intra-arterial chemotherapy after liver resection</h4>

5917<p id="_1002" tabindex="-1">

5918Hepatic intra-arterial chemotherapy with floxuridine for liver metastases has produced higher overall response rates but no consistent improvement in

5919survival when compared with systemic chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.84">

592084</a>

5921,<a href="#cit/section_8.104">

5922104</a>

5923-<a href="#cit/section_8.108">

5924108</a>

5925] Controversy regarding

5926the efficacy of regional chemotherapy was the basis of a large,

5927multicenter, phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00002716">

5928Leuk-9481</a>

5929 [NCT00002716]) of hepatic arterial infusion versus

5930systemic chemotherapy. The use of combination intra-arterial

5931chemotherapy with hepatic radiation therapy, especially employing focal radiation of

5932metastatic lesions, is under evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_8.109">

5933109</a>

5934]</p>

5935<p id="_1003" tabindex="-1">

5936Several studies show increased

5937local toxic effects after hepatic infusional therapy, including liver function

5938abnormalities and fatal biliary sclerosis.</p>

5939</section>

5940</section>

5941<section id="_TrialSearch_92_sid_8">

5942<h3 id="_TrialSearch_92_sid_8_toc">

5943Current Clinical Trials</h3>

5944<p id="_TrialSearch_92_22" tabindex="-1">

5945Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

5946advanced clinical trial search</a>

5947 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

5948General information</a>

5949 about clinical trials is also available.</p>
